## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and population size, which is the right-hand side of a population dynamics ODE. Classical models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex forms involving Allee effects, theta-logistic models, and time-varying carrying capacities.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor/population models)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2 (flexible asymmetric growth)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity variation)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic growth model with multiple equilibria)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield harvesting)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying intrinsic growth rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth with linear death)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt ~ c*P) → exponential/Malthusian regime with no density regulation
- Quadratic term in P (dP_dt ~ c0*P - c1*P²) → logistic-type density-dependent regulation with single carrying capacity
- Cubic polynomial in P (dP_dt ~ P*(P-a)*(K-P)) → Allee effect with bistability and critical population threshold
- Logarithmic dependence log(c/P) → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Trigonometric time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Ratio P/(1+c*P) → contest competition or interference among individuals limiting per-capita resources
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-limited growth or metabolic scaling (e.g., 2/3 or 3/4 power)
- Product P*f(t) → separable time-modulated growth where intrinsic rate varies with time independently of density
- Difference of power laws (c0*P^a - c1*P^b) → competing anabolic and catabolic processes with different scaling
- Constant additive/subtractive term independent of P → external immigration, harvesting, or stocking effects
